This method:\\n  1. Calls self.as_sql() to get the SQL string and parameters (line 1618)\\n  2. Gets a database cursor from the connection (line 1629)\\n  3. Executes the SQL via cursor.execute(sql, params) at line 1631—THIS IS WHERE OperationalError IS RAISED if the database is unavailable or encounters an error.\\n\\n**Execution Flow:**\\nUser builds QuerySet → QuerySet is lazy → User iterates QuerySet → QuerySet.__iter__() calls _fetch_all() → ModelIterable created and iterated → ModelIterable.__iter__() calls compiler.execute_sql() → execute_sql() compiles SQL via as_sql() → cursor.execute() runs against database → OperationalError raised if database issue occurs.\\n\\nThe key architectural insight is that Django maintains laziness by deferring both SQL compilation (as_sql is only called when needed) and database execution (cursor.execute is only called during iteration) until the queryset results are actually required.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
